[Pratyan╠Дgirasa.тАФdv─Бtriс╣Е┼Ыat. kс╣Ыty─Бd┼лс╣гaс╣Зadevatyam. ─Бnuс╣гс╣нubham: 1. mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 2. vir─Бс╣З n─Бma g─Бyatr─л; 9. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti; 12. pan╠Дkti; 13. urobс╣Ыhat─л; 15. 4-p. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 17, 20, 24. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti (20. vir─Бj); 16, 18. triс╣гс╣нubh; 19. 4-p. jagat─л; 22. 1-av. 2-p. ─Бrcy uс╣гс╣Зih; 23. 3-p. bhurig viс╣гam─Б g─Бyatr─л; 28. 3-p. g─Бyatr─л; 29. madhyejyotiс╣гmat─л jagat─л; 32. dvyanuс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б 5-p. atijagat─л.]

Whitney

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. The hymn (vs. 1) is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 39. 7, with several others, in a ceremony against witchcraft, and several of its verses or parts of verses elsewhere. The V─Бit. uses only one half-verse (21 c, d).

Translations

Translated: Ludwig, p. 520; Henry, i, 39; Griffith, ii. 1; Bloomfield, 72, 602.

Griffith

A charm against witchcraft

Translation
  1. She whom the adepts {cikits├║) prepare, all-formed, hand-made, like
    a bride at a weddingтАФlet her go far off; we push her away.
Notes

‘She,’ because kс╣Ыty─Б ‘witchcraft’ is feminine. The name, mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л,
given to the verse, is improperly applied, тМКif we understand it as
defined by RV. Pr─Бt. xvi. 48: here is meant rather that defined as of
three j─Бgata p─Бdas (12 + 12: 11) at Ind. Stud. viii. 243тМЛ.

Griffith

Afar let her depart: away we drive her whom, made with hands, all-beautiful, Skilled men prepare and fashion like a bride amid her nuptial train.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who said to thee “go forth,” against the current, up-stream, him,
    O witchcraft, do thou return against; seek not us who are innocent.
Notes

Of this verse is legible in Ppp. ud─Бyyam in b; as for our mss.,
they cannot be relied upon in the least to distinguish pya and yya,
but the majority rather favor ud─Бyy├аm, while P. reads -─Бryy├аm, D.
-─Бjy├аm (?), W. -─Бhyam. Neither word has been found anywhere else,
but doubtless ud─Бpy├аm is the true form.

Griffith

Whoever said to thee, Go forth against the foeman up the stream, To him, O Kritya, go thou back. Pursue not us, the sinless ones.

  1. He who put together thy joints, as an с╣Ыbh├║ [those] of a chariot

Griffith

He who composed thy limbs with thought as a deft joiner builds a car, Go to him: thither lies thy way. This man is all unknown to thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They who, having made, took hold of thee, cunning sorcerersтАФthis is a
    healthful (┼Ыambh├║) spoiler of witchcraft, counteracting, reverting;
    therewith do we bathe thee.
Notes

The address changes, as often elsewhere, from the witchcraft to the
bewitched person. Ppp. reads, in c, vidma for ┼Ыambhu, and, in
d, pratisaram. Our text ought to read in c ┼Ыambhv ├мd├бm,
although all the mss. happen to agree here in lengthening the i.

Griffith

The cunning men, the sorcerers who fashioned thee and held thee fast,– This cures and mars their witchery, this, repellent, drives it back the way it came. With this we make thee swim.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In that they have taken (grah) the name of thee giving to the
    Fathers, or at the sacrificeтАФlet these plants free thee from all ill
    that is designed (? saс╣Бde┼Ыy├а).
Notes

It might be also (in a, b) ’those giving to the Fathers have taken
the name of thee’ (Ludwig, ’thy Fathers’). Saс╣Бde┼Ыy├а is very obscure.
The first half-verse is wholly corrupt in Ppp.

Griffith

If, as they gave thy parents aught, they named thee, or at sacri- fice, From all their purposed evil let these healing herbs deliver thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. From sin against the gods, against the Fathers, from name-taking,
    that is designed, that is devised against [any one], let the plants
    free thee by their energy (v─лry├а), with spell (br├бhman), with
    verses, with milk of the seers.
Notes

‘Milk’ (p├бyas) in the last p─Бda looks like a corrupt reading, but Ppp.
appears to have the same; Bp.E. accent payas─Б╠Б. тМКAs for the
combinations of -─Б с╣Ы-, see note to Pr─Бt. iii. 46.тМЛ Several mss.
(Bp.O.p.m.R.T.K.) read pitry─Б╠Аt in a. The verse, which ought to be
called an anuс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б triс╣гс╣нubh (11 + 8: 11 + 11 = 41), is very
foolishly described by the Anukr. as a pan╠Дkti, because it contains
nearly (and can easily be reduced to precisely) 40 syllables.

Griffith

From mention of thy name, from sin against the Fathers or the Gods, These herbs of healing shall by prayer release thee, by power, by holy texts, the milk of .Rishis.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As the wind sets in motion the dust from the earth and the cloud
    (abhr├б) from the atmosphere, so from me may everything of evil nature
    go away, pushed by the spell (br├бhman).
Notes
Griffith

As the wind stirs the dust from earth and drives the rain cloud from the sky, So, chased and banished by the spell, all misery departs from me.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Step away, making much noise, like an unfastened she-ass; attain
    thy makers, pushed hence by an energetic spell.
Notes

Some of the mss. (O.p.m.K.) read kartr├йn in c, as in other such
cases.

Griffith

Go with a resonant cry, depart, like a she-ass whose cords are loosed. Go to thy makers: hence! away! Go driven by the potent spell.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Saying “this is the road, O witchcraft,” we conduct thee; thee that
    wast sent forth against [us] we send forth back again; by that
    [road] go against [them], breaking, like a draft-cow with a cart,
    all-formed, wearing a wreath (? kur┼лс╣н├нn).
Notes

The last word is found only here, and has to be rendered conjecturally
(with the Pet. Lexx.). All the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. тМКor rather, most of them:
see also note to Pr─Бt. iii. 35тМЛ combine kс╣Ыty├й тАЩti тМКand thus indeed the
meter requires us to pronounceтМЛ; but our edition restores the more
correct reading тМКkс╣Ыtya ├нtiтМЛ, since the Pr─Бt. does not countenance the
irregularity; we should expect to find it with vandane тАЩva (in ii.
56). Ppp. reads at the beginning ayaс╣Б panth─Б тАЩpinay─Бmi tv─Б kс╣Ыtye
prahit─Бс╣Б prati etc.; in c тМКor rather c-dтМЛ, tu├▒jaty anasvin─л
тАЩva. In the Anukr. it seems as if catuс╣гpad─Б. must be a misreading for
pa├▒capad─Б (11 + 11: 8 + 8 + 8 = 46): but compare vs. 19.

Griffith

This, Kritya, is thy path, we say, and guide thee. We drive thee back who hast been sent against us. Go by this pathway, breaking loose for onslaught even as a host complete with cars and horses.

резрем рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрддреЗ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд░рдкрдердореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Offward is light for thee, hitherward is no road for thee; make thy
    goings elsewhere than [toward] us; go thou by a distant [road]
    beyond ninety difficult navigable streams; do not wound thyself; go
    away.
Notes

One would like to emend kс╣гaс╣Зiс╣гс╣нh─Бs in d, perhaps to kс╣гamiс╣гс╣нh─Бs
‘be patient’ i.e. ’linger’; Ppp. has instead gh─Бniс╣гс╣нh─Бs, which
unfortunately gives no help. Ppp. also combines n─Бvy─Б тАЩti in c;
and the description of the Anukr. appears to sanction it.

Griffith

No path leads hitherward for thee to travel. Turn thee from us: far off, thy light is yonder. Fly hence across the ninety floods, the rivers most hard to pass. Begone, and be not wounded.

резрен рд╡рд╛рдд рдЗрд╡ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. As the wind the trees, do thou crush (mс╣Ы) down, cause to fall; do
    not leave of them cow, horse, man; turning back, O witchcraft, from here
    to thy makers, awaken them unto childlessness.
Notes

Here, in c, even a majority of the mss. (W.I.O.D.T.K.) read
kartr├йn. Ppp. combines at the beginning v─Бte тАЩva, as the meter
demands, and as the Anukr. assumes; ├║chiс╣г─Бi тАЩс╣г─Бm is doubtless also the
real reading in b.

Griffith

As wind the trees, so smite and overthrow them: leave not cow, horse, or man of them surviving Return, O Kritya, unto those who made thee. Wake them from sleep to find that they are childless.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What [witchcraft] they buried for thee in the barh├нs, what in
    the cemetery, [what] witchcraft or secret spell (valag├б) in the
    field, or practised against thee in the householders’ fireтАФthey, being
    wiser, [against thee] who art simple, innocent.
Notes

Ppp. helps both meter and sense by inserting cakrus before barhiс╣гi
in a; it also arranges kс╣Ыty─Бс╣Б kс╣гetre in b, combines dh─лratar─Б
тАЩn─Бg- at the end, and adds, to complete the verse, tam тМКso Roth’s
Collation! for t─Бm?тМЛ ito n─Б┼Ыay─Бmasi. The Anukr. notices neither the
deficiency in a nor the redundancy in d.

Griffith

The charm or secret power which they have buried for thee in sacred grass, field, cemetery, Or spell in household fire which men more cunning have wrought against thee innocent and simple,–

Translation
  1. We have found out (anu-vid) the hostile sneaking magic (?
    k├бrtra) that was applied, perceived (? anu-budh), buried: let that
    go whence it was brought; there let it roll about like a horse; let it
    slay the progeny of the witchcraft -maker.
Notes

тАЩva, as called for by the meter. The Anukr. is as bad in its treatment
of this verse as of 15.

Griffith

That tool of hatred, understood, made ready, stealthy and buried deep, have we discovered, Let that go back to whence it came, turn thither like a horse and kill the children of the sorcerer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. There are knives of good metal in our house; we know thy joints, O
    witchcraft, how many they are; just stand up; go away from here; unknown
    one, what seekest thou here?
Notes

That is, ’thou who art no acquaintance of ours.’ The Anukr. is much more
scrupulous than usual in calling the verse (12 + 11: 8 + 8 = 39) vir─Бj
тМКscanning a perhaps as 11тМЛ. Ppp. begins with svayas─Б. The third p─Бda
is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 39. 19.

Griffith

Within our house are swords of goodly iron. Kritya, we know thy joints and all their places. Arise this instant and begone! What, stranger! art thou seek- ing here?

Translation
  1. Thy neck-bones (gr─лv─Б╠Б), O witchcraft, and thy (two) feet I will
    cut up; run thou out; let Indra-and-Agni defend us, they who are of

Notes

Praj─Б╠Бvat─л at the end looks like a corruption of praj─Б╠Бpat─л, which
Ppp. reads тМКR’s collation has prajapat─лтМЛ. Ppp. also has in c en─Бс╣Б
vс╣Ы┼Ыcat─Б. But K─Бu┼Ы., which quotes the last half-verse in full in 5. 2,
reads praj─Бvat─л. The same half-verse appears also by prat─лka in
V─Бit. 8. 6 (unless V─Бit. takes it rather from K─Бu┼Ы.).

O Kritya, I will cut thy throat and hew thy feet off. Run, be- gone! Indra and Agni, Guardian Lords of living creatures, shield us well!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Anointed, smeared, well-adorned, bearing all difficulty, go thou
    away; recognize (j├▒─Б), O witchcraft, thy maker, as a daughter her own
    father.
Notes

The definition of this verse appears to be omitted in the Anukr., as we
can hardly be meant to take it for an anuс╣гс╣нubh. The first p─Бda is
capable of being crowded together into 8 syllables, or expanded into 12
(either procedure being about equally strained), making the verse either
an urobс╣Ыhat─л or a prast─Бrapan╠Дkti. It is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 39. 18.

Griffith

Anointed, balmed, and well adorned, bearing all trouble with thee, go. Even as a daughter knows her sire, so know thy marker, Kritya, thou.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go away, O witchcraft; stand not; lead, as it were, the track of one
    pierced; it is a deer, thou a deer-hunter; it is unable to put thee
    down.
Notes

‘Lead,’ in b, appears to be used in the sense of ‘follow’; the
’track’ is doubtless that of the maker: тМКcf. note to xi. 2. 13тМЛ. The
pada-text divides mс╣Ыgaре░y├║с╕е: cf. Pr─Бt. iii. 18.

Griffith

Kritya, begone, stay not. Pursue as ’twere the wounded crea- ture’s track. He is the chase, the hunter thou he may not slight or humble thee.

реирен рдЙрдд рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Also the after one (├бpara) slays with an arrow, fitting it (?),
    the one shooting (-─Бsin) in front; also of the front one, smiting
    down, the after one smites down in return.
Notes

This obscure and probably corrupt verse gets no help from Ppp., which
merely reads uto for uta in c. The Pet. Lex. suggests emendation
of -d─Б╠Бya to -dh─Б╠Бya in b, and the translation implies the change.

Griffith

He waits, and aiming with his shaft smites him who first would shoot at him, And, when the foeman deals a blow before him, following strikes him down.

Translation
  1. Hear thou, verily, these words of mine; then go whence thou camest,

Hearken to this my word; then go thither away whence thou hast come; to him who made thee go thou back.

реиреп рдЕрдирд╛рдЧреЛрд╣рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡реИ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The slaying of an innocent person is indeed fearful, O witchcraft;
    slay thou not our cow, horse, man; wheresoever thou art set down, from
    there we make thee stand up; become thou lighter than a leaf.
Notes

The pada-text has in d ├║t: sth─Бp-; the example of the omitted
s is quoted under Pr─Бt. ii. 18. The verse (10+ 10: 8 + 8 + 8 = 44) is
very badly defined by the Anukr. Ppp. reads in a -hatyam and
bh─лmam.

Griffith

The slaughter of an innocent, O Kritya, is an awful deed. Slay not cow, horse, or man of ours. In whatsoever place thou art concealed we rouse thee up there- from: become thou lighter than a leaf.

Translation
  1. If ye are covered (─Б-vс╣Ы) with darkness, like those who are girt
    (abhi-dh─Б) with a netтАФhaving torn up (sam-lup) all witchcrafts from

Griffith

If ye be girt about with clouds of darkness, bound as with a net. We rend and tear all witcheries hence and to their maker send them back.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The progeny of the witchcraft-maker, of him of secret spells, of him
    that devises against [others], O witchcraft, do thou kill; do not
    leave [them alive]; slay yonder witchcraft-makers.
Notes

Ppp. uses the singular in d.

Griffith

The brood of wizard, sorcerer, the purposer of evil deed. Crush thou, O Kritya spare not, kill those practisers of magic arts.

рейреи рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. As the sun is freed out of darkness, [and] quits the night and the
    ensigns of the dawn, so do I quit all evil-natured magic made by the
    witchcraft-maker, as an elephant the difficult haze (? r├бjas).
Notes

Ppp. puts tamasas before mucyate in a, reads ketum at end of
b, and omits d altogether. The verse (12 + 11: 8 + 8 + 11 = 50)
lacks two syllables of being a full atijagat─л (52). The prat─лka
(yath─Б s┼лrya) is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 39. 26; but the comm. regards vii.
13. 1, and not this, as the verse intended.

тМКThe quoted Anukr. says dve (i.e. 2 above the norm of 30).тМЛ

Griffith

As Surya frees himself from depth of darkness, and casts away the night and rays of morning, So I repel each baleful charm which an enchanter hath pre- pared; And, as an elephant shakes off the dust, I cast the plague aside.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдп рджрдгреНрдб рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ред

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдерд╛) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп (рддрдорд╕рдГ рдкрд░рд┐) рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ) рдЫреБрдЯрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдореН) (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ) рдЙрд╖рд╛ [рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рдд рд╕рдордп] рдХреЗ (рдХреЗрддреВрдиреН) рдЪрд┐рд╣реНрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЬрд╣рд╛рддрд┐) рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рдПрд╡) рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА (рдЕрд╣рдореН) рдореИрдВ (рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдХреГрддрд╛) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд░рдХреЗ (рдХреГрддрдореН) рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН) рд╕рдм (рджреБрд░реНрднреВрддрдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ (рдХрд░реНрддреНрд░рдореН) рдХрд░реНрдо рдХреЛ (рдЬрд╣рд╛рдорд┐) рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ, (рдЗрд╡) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рд╣рд╕реНрддреА) рд╣рд╛рдереА (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрдореН) рдХрдард┐рди (рд░рдЬрдГ) рджреЗрд╢ рдХреЛ [рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ] реерейреирее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдХреЛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ рдЕрдкрдиреА рддреАрд╡реНрд░ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЛрдВ рдХреА рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рд╣рдЯрд╛рдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╣рд╛рдереА рдХрдард┐рди рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерейреирее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рейреитИТ(рдпрдерд╛, рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ) (рдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ) рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ (рддрдорд╕рдГ) рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН (рдкрд░рд┐) рдкреГрдердХреН (рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдореН) (рдЬрд╣рд╛рддрд┐) рддреНрдпрдЬрддрд┐ (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ) рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рддрд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ (рдЪ) (рдХреЗрддреВрдиреН) рдЪрд┐рд╣реНрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдПрд╡) рддрдерд╛ (рдЕрд╣рдореН) (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН) (рджреБрд░реНрднреВрддрдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдореН (рдХрд░реНрддреНрд░рдореН) рдХрд░реЛрддреЗрдГ рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рдиреНред рдХрд░реНрдо (рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдХреГрддрд╛) рдореж реиред рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрд╛ (рдХреГрддрдореН) рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрдореН (рд╣рд╕реНрддреА, рдЗрд╡) (рд░рдЬрдГ) рд▓реЛрдХрдореН-рдирд┐рд░реБреж рекредрезрепред рджреЗрд╢рдореН (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрдореН) рджреБрд░реНрдЧрдордиреАрдпрдореН (рдЬрд╣рд╛рдорд┐) рддреНрдпрдЬрд╛рдорд┐ рее
